## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / kinetic ODE modeling)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is an ordinary differential equation for the time evolution of a concentration A(t), which is the standard setup for chemical reaction kinetics. With only t and A available, the most likely relationships are classical kinetic rate laws where dA_dt depends on A (order, saturation, equilibrium) and possibly explicit time-dependence (changing conditions, catalyst activity, feeding).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption/production: dA_dt = c0 (constant-rate regime, e.g., surface-limited with excess reactant)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = c0 * A (elementary unimolecular step; sign of c0 determines decay vs growth)
- Offset first-order (approach to steady state): dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A (source/sink plus linear loss, CSTR-like lumping)
- Second-order / bimolecular in A: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (self-reaction/dimerization or effective second-order under lumping)
- General nth-order law: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (empirical overall reaction order)
- Reversible linear relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) (net rate proportional to driving force to A = c1)
- Logistic/autocatalytic with depletion: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (autocatalysis with limiting capacity/consumption)
- Gompertz-type kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * log(c1 * A) (sigmoidal-in-time concentration evolution in some empirical kinetics)
- Saturating (diffusion/transport-limited) decay: dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (rate increases ~A at low A, plateaus at high A)
- Product-inhibition-like form: dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A**c2) (stronger inhibition/saturation with adjustable steepness)
- Time-varying rate constant (deactivation/aging): dA_dt = c0 * A / (t + c1) (effective rate slows down with time, e.g., catalyst deactivation lumping)
- Exponentially drifting conditions: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (rate accelerates/decays due to changing environment lumped into k(t))
- Periodic forcing (e.g., light-driven or oscillatory feed): dA_dt = c0 * A * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) (time-modulated kinetics)
- Mixed source + nonlinear loss: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A - c2 * A**2 (birth–death style kinetics; steady-state from balance)
- Rational approach to equilibrium with nonlinear loss: dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) / (1 + c2 * A) (driving-force form with saturation/inhibition)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt is proportional to A, the trajectory A(t) is exponential in time (signature of first-order kinetics).
- If dA_dt is approximately constant over a range of A, it indicates a zero-order regime (surface/photochemical limitation or reactant in large excess).
- Quadratic dependence (A**2) suggests bimolecular/self-reaction or an effective second-order step dominating the dynamics.
- A driving-force form (c1 - A) implies relaxation toward an equilibrium/steady concentration c1 (common for reversible or exchange processes).
- A*(c1 - A) produces sigmoidal transients and a stable fixed point at A = c1 (autocatalysis with depletion/limitation).
- Rational saturation in A (A/(1+c*A)) indicates transport limitation, site saturation, or inhibition causing diminishing returns at high concentration.
- Explicit time dependence in the coefficient (e.g., 1/(t+c), exp(c*t), sin(c*t)) indicates nonstationary conditions such as catalyst deactivation, changing illumination, or periodic feed.
- A constant term plus a loss term (c0 + c1*A or c0 - c1*A) indicates simultaneous feed/production and consumption, leading to a nonzero steady state.
- Log terms (A*log(...)) often encode empirically observed asymmetric sigmoids (slow start, rapid mid-course, long tail) compared with logistic forms.
